The Obligation of Responding to Salam and the Preferred Wording
Ruling on responding to salam with reward and phrasing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that responding to salam is wajib, explain why the responder gets more reward, and recall the preferred response with the waw.

Core Idea
Responding to salam is wajib, not fard; the responder earns more reward, and the best response includes 'wa alaykum' with the waw.

In the Hanafi school, greeting with salam is a highly recommended sunnah, but responding is an obligation that carries great reward. This lesson clarifies the legal status of the response and the preferred phrasing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is 'responding to salam'. The text states it is 'wajib'. Identify the ruling level as wajib (obligatory, but not fard).
In Hanafi fiqh, wajib is an obligation established by zanni dalil; fard is established by qat'i dalil.
2
Distinguish between initiator and responder
The text notes a difference of opinion over which is better. The chosen view is that the responder has more reward.
This is based on the idea that the responder fulfills an obligation.
3
Learn the preferred wording
The best response includes the waw ('and') and adds 'wa rahmatullahi wa barakatuh'. The phrase 'وعليكم السلام' is preferred over 'عليكم السلام'.
The waw is a sunnah addition.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) consider responding as fard kifayah. In Hanafi, it is wajib, meaning it is still sinful to omit but not as severe as neglecting a fard.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رجل يدعوه الأمير فيسأله عن أشياء فيتكلم بما يوافق الحق يناله منه المكروه لا ينبغي له أن يتكلم إلا بالحق إلا أن يخاف القتل أو إتلاف عضو وأن يأخذ ماله. ولو مر على قوم وفيهم أهل الذمة أو كافر قال بعضهم يقول السلام على من ابتع الهدى، والصحيح أنه يقول السلام عليكم وينوي المسلمين في قلبه وفي التتارخانية : إذا استقبل المسلم أخاه فسلم عليه يخرج من ذنوبه كيوم ولدته أمه، وفي النوازل : إذا أتى بيت غيره لا يدخل حتى يؤذن له، فإن أذن له يدخل ويسلم عليه. ورد السلام واجب واختلفوا في أيهما أفضل البادئ أو الراد الراد أكثر أجراً والأفضل أن يأتي بالواو بأن يقول وعليكم السلام ورحمة الله وبركاته. وفي فتاوى أهواز : السلام سنة على الراكب للراجل في طريق عام أو مفازة فإذا التقيا فأفضلهما الأسبق بالسلام، فإذا التقى الرجل بالمرأة يبدأ الرجل بالسلام، وإن بدأت فيرد عليها السلام إن كانت عجوزاً فبلسانه، وإن كانت شابة فبالإشارة. قال الفقيه أبو الليث : إذا دخل الفقيه على غيره ولم يسلم أثموا. وفي الغياثية : يكره السلام بالسبابة والسنة أن يسلم عليهم بلفظ الجمع، ولو كان المسلم عليه واحداً واختلفوا في السلام على الصبيان قال بعضهم لا يسلم وهو قول الحسن، وقال بعضهم يسلم هو الأفضل وبه أخذ الفقيه أبو الليث، وإذا رد واحد من القوم السلام سقط الباقين. وفي الصيرفية : دخل على زوجته لا يسلم عليها بل هي تسلم عليه فإن لم يكن في البيت أحد فيقول السلام علينا وعلى عباد الله الصالحين ولو على المقابر يقول السلام عليكم أنتم لنا سلف ونحن لكم تبع .اهـ. وفي الخانية : ويكره أن يسلم على من هو في الخلاء ولا يرد عليه السلام. وكذا الأكل والقارئ والمشتغل بالعلم وكذا في الحمام إن كان مكشوف العورة .
A man whom the ruler calls and asks about things; he speaks the truth, and receives harm from it. He should not speak except the truth, unless he fears death, loss of a limb, or taking of his wealth. If he passes by a group including dhimmis or a disbeliever, some say he should say 'Peace be upon those who follow guidance.' The correct view is that he says 'Peace be upon you' and intends the Muslims in his heart. In al-Tatarkhaniyya: When a Muslim meets his brother and greets him, his sins fall off like the day his mother gave birth to him. In al-Nawazil: When he comes to another's house, he should not enter until permission is given. If permission is given, he enters and greets. Responding to the greeting is obligatory. They differed over which is better: the initiator or the responder. The responder has greater reward. It is better to include the waw (and) by saying 'And upon you be peace, and the mercy of Allah and His blessings.' In Fatawa Ahwaz: Greeting is sunnah for the rider to the pedestrian on a public road or desert. When they meet, the better of them is the one who initiates the greeting. When a man meets a woman, the man initiates the greeting. If she initiates, he responds to her greeting: if she is an old woman, verbally; if she is a young woman, by gesture. Al-Faqih Abu al-Layth said: When a scholar enters upon others and does not greet, they all sin. In al-Ghiyathiyya: It is disliked to greet with the index finger. The sunnah is to greet them with the plural form, even if the one being greeted is one. They differed about greeting children. Some said do not greet, which is the view of al-Hasan. Some said greeting is better, and al-Faqih Abu al-Layth adopted this. When one of the group responds to the greeting, it suffices for the rest. In al-Sayrafiyya: If he enters upon his wife, he should not greet her, but she greets him. If there is no one in the house, he says 'Peace be upon us and upon the righteous slaves of Allah.' And upon graves, he says 'Peace be upon you, you are our predecessors and we are your followers.' End. In al-Khaniyya: It is disliked to greet someone who is relieving himself, and he should not respond. Likewise, one who is eating, reading, or engaged in knowledge. Also in the bathhouse if the private parts are uncovered.
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings on the etiquette and legal obligations of greeting (salam). It begins with a scenario where a man is summoned by a ruler and must speak truth despite harm, except when fearing death, loss of limb, or wealth. Then rulings on greeting dhimmis: the correct view is to say 'Peace be upon you' intending Muslims. The text then cites various sources: greeting a Muslim brother causes sins to fall off; entering a house requires permission and then greeting; responding to salam is wajib (obligatory); the responder gets more reward; it is sunnah to use the full phrasing with 'and' on the return. The rider should greet the pedestrian; the best is the one who initiates. For a man and woman, man initiates, but if woman initiates, man responds verbally if she is old, by gesture if young. A scholar should greet when entering, otherwise all sin. Greeting with the index finger is disliked, and the plural form is sunnah even for one person. Greeting children: better to greet. One response suffices for a group. When entering upon his wife, she greets him, not vice versa; if alone, say 'Peace be upon us and righteous slaves.' At graves, a specific greeting is said. It is disliked to greet or respond to one who is relieving himself, eating, reading, studying, or in the bathhouse if private parts are uncovered. These rulings show the comprehensive nature of Islamic etiquette in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
السلام (al-salam): The Islamic greeting; initiating is sunnah, responding is wajib.
الواو (al-waw): The conjunction 'and' used in the response 'wa alaykum' to indicate inclusion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the reward of the responder compared to the initiator?
A) The initiator gets more reward
B) The responder gets more reward
C) Both get equal reward
D) Only the initiator gets reward

Key Takeaway
Responding to salam is wajib, the responder gets more reward, and the best response includes the waw.

Greeting Specific Categories: Dhimmis, Children, Wife, and Graves
Rulings on greeting specific individuals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the proper way to greet dhimmis, children, one's wife, and the deceased, and explain the reasoning behind each ruling.

Core Idea
The greeting of salam is adapted to specific contexts: for dhimmis, intend Muslims; for children, greet them; for wife, she greets first; for graves, use a specific phrase.

The general rule of greeting with salam is flexible to accommodate different situations. This lesson covers four special cases: greeting non-Muslims, children, one's spouse, and the dead. Each has its own etiquette and ruling.

Guided Path
1
Greeting Dhimmis
When passing by a group that includes dhimmis or disbelievers, the correct view is to say 'Assalamu alaykum' and intend the Muslims in your heart. Some say to use a modified greeting, but the chosen view is the general greeting with intention.
Intention distinguishes the addressees.
2
Greeting Children
There is a difference of opinion. The preferred view (taken by al-Faqih Abu al-Layth) is that it is better to greet children, as it teaches them etiquette.
This is sunnah.
3
Greeting One's Wife
When entering upon his wife, the husband does not initiate the greeting; rather, the wife greets him. This is based on submission and beautiful conduct.
If alone in the house, one says 'Peace be upon us and upon the righteous slaves of Allah'.
4
Greeting at Graves
When visiting graves, one says 'Peace be upon you, you are our predecessors and we are your followers'. This acknowledges the dead and reminds of the afterlife.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رجل يدعوه الأمير فيسأله عن أشياء فيتكلم بما يوافق الحق يناله منه المكروه لا ينبغي له أن يتكلم إلا بالحق إلا أن يخاف القتل أو إتلاف عضو وأن يأخذ ماله. ولو مر على قوم وفيهم أهل الذمة أو كافر قال بعضهم يقول السلام على من ابتع الهدى، والصحيح أنه يقول السلام عليكم وينوي المسلمين في قلبه وفي التتارخانية : إذا استقبل المسلم أخاه فسلم عليه يخرج من ذنوبه كيوم ولدته أمه، وفي النوازل : إذا أتى بيت غيره لا يدخل حتى يؤذن له، فإن أذن له يدخل ويسلم عليه. ورد السلام واجب واختلفوا في أيهما أفضل البادئ أو الراد الراد أكثر أجراً والأفضل أن يأتي بالواو بأن يقول وعليكم السلام ورحمة الله وبركاته. وفي فتاوى أهواز : السلام سنة على الراكب للراجل في طريق عام أو مفازة فإذا التقيا فأفضلهما الأسبق بالسلام، فإذا التقى الرجل بالمرأة يبدأ الرجل بالسلام، وإن بدأت فيرد عليها السلام إن كانت عجوزاً فبلسانه، وإن كانت شابة فبالإشارة. قال الفقيه أبو الليث : إذا دخل الفقيه على غيره ولم يسلم أثموا. وفي الغياثية : يكره السلام بالسبابة والسنة أن يسلم عليهم بلفظ الجمع، ولو كان المسلم عليه واحداً واختلفوا في السلام على الصبيان قال بعضهم لا يسلم وهو قول الحسن، وقال بعضهم يسلم هو الأفضل وبه أخذ الفقيه أبو الليث، وإذا رد واحد من القوم السلام سقط الباقين. وفي الصيرفية : دخل على زوجته لا يسلم عليها بل هي تسلم عليه فإن لم يكن في البيت أحد فيقول السلام علينا وعلى عباد الله الصالحين ولو على المقابر يقول السلام عليكم أنتم لنا سلف ونحن لكم تبع .اهـ. وفي الخانية : ويكره أن يسلم على من هو في الخلاء ولا يرد عليه السلام. وكذا الأكل والقارئ والمشتغل بالعلم وكذا في الحمام إن كان مكشوف العورة .
A man whom the ruler calls and asks about things; he speaks the truth, and receives harm from it. He should not speak except the truth, unless he fears death, loss of a limb, or taking of his wealth. If he passes by a group including dhimmis or a disbeliever, some say he should say 'Peace be upon those who follow guidance.' The correct view is that he says 'Peace be upon you' and intends the Muslims in his heart. In al-Tatarkhaniyya: When a Muslim meets his brother and greets him, his sins fall off like the day his mother gave birth to him. In al-Nawazil: When he comes to another's house, he should not enter until permission is given. If permission is given, he enters and greets. Responding to the greeting is obligatory. They differed over which is better: the initiator or the responder. The responder has greater reward. It is better to include the waw (and) by saying 'And upon you be peace, and the mercy of Allah and His blessings.' In Fatawa Ahwaz: Greeting is sunnah for the rider to the pedestrian on a public road or desert. When they meet, the better of them is the one who initiates the greeting. When a man meets a woman, the man initiates the greeting. If she initiates, he responds to her greeting: if she is an old woman, verbally; if she is a young woman, by gesture. Al-Faqih Abu al-Layth said: When a scholar enters upon others and does not greet, they all sin. In al-Ghiyathiyya: It is disliked to greet with the index finger. The sunnah is to greet them with the plural form, even if the one being greeted is one. They differed about greeting children. Some said do not greet, which is the view of al-Hasan. Some said greeting is better, and al-Faqih Abu al-Layth adopted this. When one of the group responds to the greeting, it suffices for the rest. In al-Sayrafiyya: If he enters upon his wife, he should not greet her, but she greets him. If there is no one in the house, he says 'Peace be upon us and upon the righteous slaves of Allah.' And upon graves, he says 'Peace be upon you, you are our predecessors and we are your followers.' End. In al-Khaniyya: It is disliked to greet someone who is relieving himself, and he should not respond. Likewise, one who is eating, reading, or engaged in knowledge. Also in the bathhouse if the private parts are uncovered.
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings on the etiquette and legal obligations of greeting (salam). It begins with a scenario where a man is summoned by a ruler and must speak truth despite harm, except when fearing death, loss of limb, or wealth. Then rulings on greeting dhimmis: the correct view is to say 'Peace be upon you' intending Muslims. The text then cites various sources: greeting a Muslim brother causes sins to fall off; entering a house requires permission and then greeting; responding to salam is wajib (obligatory); the responder gets more reward; it is sunnah to use the full phrasing with 'and' on the return. The rider should greet the pedestrian; the best is the one who initiates. For a man and woman, man initiates, but if woman initiates, man responds verbally if she is old, by gesture if young. A scholar should greet when entering, otherwise all sin. Greeting with the index finger is disliked, and the plural form is sunnah even for one person. Greeting children: better to greet. One response suffices for a group. When entering upon his wife, she greets him, not vice versa; if alone, say 'Peace be upon us and righteous slaves.' At graves, a specific greeting is said. It is disliked to greet or respond to one who is relieving himself, eating, reading, studying, or in the bathhouse if private parts are uncovered. These rulings show the comprehensive nature of Islamic etiquette in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
أهل الذمة (ahl al-dhimma): Non-Muslim citizens of an Islamic state.
السلام على الصبيان (al-salam 'ala al-sibyan): Greeting children; Hanafi: it is better to greet them.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When entering upon his wife, who should initiate the greeting according to the Hanafi school?
A) The husband
B) The wife
C) Both greet simultaneously
D) No greeting is given

Key Takeaway
Greeting specific categories requires awareness of context: intention for dhimmis, preference for children, wife-initiated, and appropriate address for graves.

beginner
5 min
Situations Where Greeting is Disliked
Rulings on disliked situations for greeting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify situations where greeting or responding to salam is disliked (makruh) in the Hanafi school and explain why.

Core Idea
Greeting is disliked when the other person is unable to respond properly or is in a state of ritual impurity or distraction.

Salam is a beautiful sunnah, but there are times when it is better to withhold it. The Hanafi school outlines several scenarios where initiating salam or responding is makruh tanzihi (disliked).

Guided Path
1
Identify the main situation: relieving oneself
It is disliked to greet someone who is in the toilet, and he should not respond.
To protect the sanctity of the greeting.
2
Identify other situations: eating, reading, studying
It is disliked to greet someone who is eating, reading, or engaged in knowledge (studying), as they are occupied.
This prevents interruption.
3
Identify the bathhouse situation
Greeting in the bathhouse is disliked if the private parts are uncovered.
Because of modesty.
4
Note the ruling on using the index finger
It is disliked to gesture the greeting with the index finger only; the sunnah is to use the full hand or words.
This applies when gesture replaces speech.

Source Text

رجل يدعوه الأمير فيسأله عن أشياء فيتكلم بما يوافق الحق يناله منه المكروه لا ينبغي له أن يتكلم إلا بالحق إلا أن يخاف القتل أو إتلاف عضو وأن يأخذ ماله. ولو مر على قوم وفيهم أهل الذمة أو كافر قال بعضهم يقول السلام على من ابتع الهدى، والصحيح أنه يقول السلام عليكم وينوي المسلمين في قلبه وفي التتارخانية : إذا استقبل المسلم أخاه فسلم عليه يخرج من ذنوبه كيوم ولدته أمه، وفي النوازل : إذا أتى بيت غيره لا يدخل حتى يؤذن له، فإن أذن له يدخل ويسلم عليه. ورد السلام واجب واختلفوا في أيهما أفضل البادئ أو الراد الراد أكثر أجراً والأفضل أن يأتي بالواو بأن يقول وعليكم السلام ورحمة الله وبركاته. وفي فتاوى أهواز : السلام سنة على الراكب للراجل في طريق عام أو مفازة فإذا التقيا فأفضلهما الأسبق بالسلام، فإذا التقى الرجل بالمرأة يبدأ الرجل بالسلام، وإن بدأت فيرد عليها السلام إن كانت عجوزاً فبلسانه، وإن كانت شابة فبالإشارة. قال الفقيه أبو الليث : إذا دخل الفقيه على غيره ولم يسلم أثموا. وفي الغياثية : يكره السلام بالسبابة والسنة أن يسلم عليهم بلفظ الجمع، ولو كان المسلم عليه واحداً واختلفوا في السلام على الصبيان قال بعضهم لا يسلم وهو قول الحسن، وقال بعضهم يسلم هو الأفضل وبه أخذ الفقيه أبو الليث، وإذا رد واحد من القوم السلام سقط الباقين. وفي الصيرفية : دخل على زوجته لا يسلم عليها بل هي تسلم عليه فإن لم يكن في البيت أحد فيقول السلام علينا وعلى عباد الله الصالحين ولو على المقابر يقول السلام عليكم أنتم لنا سلف ونحن لكم تبع .اهـ. وفي الخانية : ويكره أن يسلم على من هو في الخلاء ولا يرد عليه السلام. وكذا الأكل والقارئ والمشتغل بالعلم وكذا في الحمام إن كان مكشوف العورة .

General Etiquette of Giving Salam
General etiquette of giving salam in various contexts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi etiquette of salam in various social situations: rider to pedestrian, man to woman, scholar entering, and responding on behalf of a group.

Core Idea
The best in salam is the one who initiates; greeting should be adapted to the social context: rider to pedestrian, man to woman (with gesture for young), and one response suffices for a group.

Salam is not just a simple phrase; it carries social etiquettes that vary by situation. This lesson covers the proper conduct for greeting between rider and pedestrian, between men and women, for a scholar entering a gathering, and the efficiency of one response for a group.

Guided Path
1
Rider and pedestrian
The rider should initiate greeting to the pedestrian. The better of the two is the one who initiates.
The ruling is sunnah.
2
Man and woman
The man initiates greeting to a woman. If she initiates, he responds verbally to an old woman and by gesture to a young woman.
This preserves modesty.
3
Scholar entering a gathering
When a scholar (faqih) enters, he should greet; if he does not, all are sinful.
This highlights the importance of salam as a social bond.
4
Group response
If one person from a group responds to salam, it suffices for all.
Efficiency in fulfilling the wajib.
5
Plural form even for one person
It is sunnah to use the plural form (e.g., 'Assalamu alaykum') even when greeting a single person.
Includes the angels.

Source Text

If a group of ten people receives a salam, what is the minimum response required?
A) All ten must respond
B) One response suffices
C) Only the leader responds
D) No response is needed

Key Takeaway

Rulings on Sneezing, Slave's Collar, Backbiting, and Envy
Fiqh rulings on sneezing, placing a collar on a slave, backbiting, and envy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah of sneezing, explain the ruling on the slave's collar and its change over time, define backbiting and its exceptions, and evaluate the dispute on the meaning of the hadith on envy.

Core Idea
Fiqh rulings adapt: some are fixed, some change with circumstance, and some require precise definition.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents several distinct fiqh rulings. It begins with the sunnah practices for sneezing, then addresses the prohibition of placing a painful collar on a slave, citing a hadith against innovation. It later discusses backbiting, defining when it is sinful and when it is permissible, and concludes with a dispute on the hadith regarding envy, clarifying that true envy is haram while ghibtah is not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunnah elements of sneezing
List the phrases for the sneezer, the responder, and the sneezer's reply.
Sneezer says 'Alhamdulillah', responder says 'Yarhamukallah', sneezer replies with a prayer.
2
Distinguish gender-based rules for response
Note that a young woman does not respond verbally to a man's sneeze; she replies in her heart.
This follows the same principle as greeting to avoid fitna.
3
Analyze the ruling on the slave's collar
The matn states it is not permissible; the commentator explains it is haram because it is a punishment resembling that of disbelievers, citing the hadith against innovation.
The hadith: 'Every innovation is misguidance.'
4
Recognize the change in fatwa over time
Later scholars like those of al-Nihaya permitted the collar as a mark for runaways due to prevalence of running away.
This demonstrates that rulings can change with custom and need.
5
Define backbiting and its exceptions
Backbiting requires naming specific individuals. Mentioning faults out of concern, or when a person harms others, or informing the ruler is not backbiting.
The key is intent: concern vs belittling.
6
Interpret the hadith on envy
There is a dispute: some say envy is permissible in the two cases (wealth and knowledge), others say it remains haram but the hadith means if it were allowed, these would be the cases. The preferred view is that envy is always haram; wishing the same for oneself is ghibtah.
Blameworthy envy (hasad) is wishing removal of another's blessing; ghibtah is wishing for oneself without removal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشميت العاطس إذا كان خارج الصلاة السنة في حق العاطس أن يقول الحمد لله رب العالمين أو على كل حال، ولمن حضر أن يقول يرحمك الله فيرد عليه العاطس فيقول يغفر الله لك أو يهديك. وإذا عطست المرأة فلا بأس بتشميتها إلا أن تكون شابة، وإذا عطس الرجل فشمتته المرأة، فإن كانت عجوزاً يرد عليها، وإن كانت شابة يرد في قلبه والجواب في هذا كالجواب في السلام.
قال رحمه الله : ( وجعل الراية في عنق العبد أي لا يجوز ذلك. قال الشارح: وصورته أن يجعل في عنقه طوقاً مسمراً بمسمار عظيم يمنعه أن يحول رأسه وهو معتاد بین الظلمة وهو حرام لأن عقوبة الكافر تحرم كالإحراق بالنار وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام كل محدث بدعة وكل بدعة ضلالة وكل ضلالة في النار) » (۱) . قال في العيون: رجل اغتاب أهل قرية لم تكن غيبة حتى يسمي قوماً بأعيانهم. وفي فتاوى أهل سمرقند : ذكر مساوئ أخيه المسلم على وجه الاهتمام به ليس بغيبة، وعلى وجه النقص يكون غيبة، وإذا كان الرجل يصلي ويؤذي الناس بيده ولسانه لا غيبة في ذكر ما فيه، وإذا أعلم السلطان ليزجره فلا إثم عليه. واختلف أصحابنا في معنى قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم لا حسد إلا في اثنتين رجل آتاه الله تعالى مالاً فهو ينفقه في طاعة الله، ورجل آتاه الله علماً فهو يعلم الناس ويقضي به (۲) . قال شيخ الإسلام: ظاهر الحديث. إباحة الحسد في هذين الأمرين لأنه استثناء من المحرم فيكون مباحاً. وقال غيره : الحسد حرام في هذين كما هو حرام في غيرهما، وإنما معنى الحديث لو كان الحسد جائزاً لجاز في هذين ن، ومعنى الحسد المذموم أن يرى على غيره نعمة فيتمنى زوال تلك النعمة. عن ذلك الغير وتمني ذلك لنفسه، أما لو تمنى لنفسه مثلها لا يكون حسداً بل يسمى غبطه ا هـ . وفي النهاية : الراية علامة أنه آبق ولا بأس به في زماننا الغلبة الإباق خصوصاً في الهنود وكان في زمانهم مكروهاً لقلة الإباق ا هـ . وفي السراجية : ويكره أن يغل يديه ولو كان الرجل يقوم ويوزع المظالم من الإمام بالعدل والأنصاف كان مأجوراً، وإن خاف الرجل على نفسه لا بأس به.
Sneezing: When outside prayer, the sunnah for the sneezer is to say 'Alhamdulillah Rabb al-Alameen' or 'on every state.' For those present to say 'Yarhamukallah.' Then the sneezer responds by saying 'Yaghfir Allahu lak' or 'Yahdik.' If a woman sneezes, there is no harm in sneezing, unless she is young. If a man sneezes and a woman sneezes him, if she is old, he responds to her; if she is young, he responds in his heart. The answer in this is like the answer in greeting.
He (the author), may Allah have mercy on him, said: (And placing the flag on the neck of the slave, meaning it is not permissible. The commentator said: Its form is to place a collar on his neck studded with a large nail that prevents him from turning his head. This is customary among oppressors, and it is haram because punishing a disbeliever is prohibited like burning with fire. And he, peace and blessings be upon him, said: 'Every innovation is a misguidance and every misguidance is in the Fire.') He said in al-Uyun: A man backbites the people of a village; it is not backbiting until he names specific people. In Fatawa Ahl Samarqand: Mentioning the faults of a Muslim brother out of concern for him is not backbiting; if it is to belittle, it is backbiting. If a man prays and harms people with his hand and tongue, there is no backbiting in mentioning that. If he informs the ruler to restrain him, there is no sin. Our companions differed regarding the meaning of his saying, peace and blessings be upon him: 'There is no envy except in two: a man given wealth by Allah, so he spends it in obedience to Allah; and a man given knowledge by Allah, so he teaches people and judges by it.' Shaykh al-Islam said: The apparent meaning of the hadith is permission of envy in these two matters because it is an exception from the prohibition, so it is permissible. Others said: Envy is haram in these two as it is haram in others, but the meaning is: if envy were permissible, it would be permissible in these two. And the meaning of blameworthy envy is that one sees a blessing on someone else and wishes for its removal from that person and wishes it for himself. If he wishes for himself the like of it, it is not envy but is called ghibtah. End.
In al-Nihaya: The flag is a sign that he is a runaway (abaq). There is no harm in it in our time due to the prevalence of running away, especially among Hindus. In their time it was disliked due to the rarity of runaways. End. In al-Sirajiyya: It is disliked to tie his hands. If a man stands and distributes the rights from the ruler with justice and fairness, he is rewarded. If he fears for himself, there is no harm.
Source pages p. 381

Commentary
This passage covers multiple rulings. First, the etiquette of sneezing: the sneezer says 'Alhamdulillah', others respond with 'Yarhamukallah', and the sneezer replies with a prayer. For women, if she is old, verbal response is fine; if young, response in heart to avoid fitna. This matches the rules of greeting. Then the matn from Kanz al-Daqa'iq: 'And placing a flag on the neck of the slave' is not permissible. The commentator explains it as a painful collar, which is haram because it resembles punishment of disbelievers; a hadith warns against innovation. Then a discussion on backbiting: it requires naming individuals; mentioning faults out of concern is not backbiting; if a praying person harms others, mentioning it is not backbiting; informing the ruler to stop wrong is not sinful. Then a dispute on the hadith of envy: some say envy is permissible in the two cases (wealth and knowledge), others say it remains haram but if it were allowed, these would be the cases. True envy is wishing removal of a blessing from another, while wishing the same for oneself is ghibtah (praiseworthy). Then a return to the slave's collar: in later times, due to prevalence of running away (especially among Hindus), it is permissible to use a mark, though earlier it was disliked. Finally, tying hands is disliked, except in certain contexts like distributing justice from the ruler. This shows how rulings can change with time and need.

Key Terms
تشميت العاطس (tashmit al-'atis): Responding to a sneezer with supplication.
الراية (al-rayah): A flag or collar placed on a slave's neck as a mark for runaways.
الغيبة (al-ghibah): Backbiting: mentioning faults of a Muslim absent in a way he would dislike.
الحسد (al-hasad): Envy: wishing removal of a blessing from another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When it is about a whole village without naming individuals
B) When it is done out of concern for the person or informing the ruler to stop wrongdoing
C) When it is done in prayer
D) When the person being backbitten is a disbeliever

Key Takeaway
Fiqh rulings are dynamic: some are fixed (sneezing sunan), some change with need (slave's collar), and precise definitions (ghibah vs ghibtah) prevent misunderstanding of sacred texts.

Sneezing Etiquette (Tashmit al-'Atis)
Specifies the sunnah actions for sneezer and responder with an exception for young women.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three sunnah actions in sneezing etiquette and identify when a woman's sneeze is responded to verbally versus silently.

Core Idea
Sneezing etiquette is sunnah, but responding to a young woman is done silently to avoid fitna.

This lesson covers the sunnah actions related to sneezing, as outlined by the Hanafi school. You will learn what the sneezer and the hearer should say, and how the rule changes when a woman is involved, based on her age. This ruling mirrors the etiquette of returning salam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that sneezing etiquette (tashmit al-'atis) is a recommended (sunnah) act, not obligatory. The passage clearly states 'sunnah' for both the sneezer and the responder.
Sunnah means rewarded if done, but not sinful if omitted.
2
List the three-step sequence
The sneezer says 'Alhamdulillah' (praise to Allah). The hearer responds 'Yarhamukallah' (may Allah have mercy on you). Then the sneezer replies 'Yaghfirullahu lak' or 'Yahdeek' (may Allah forgive or guide you).
The sneezer's initial praise and final response are both sunnah.
3
Apply the exception for women
If a woman sneezes, it is permissible to respond with 'Yarhamukallah' unless she is young (shabbah). For a young woman, responding verbally is discouraged to avoid temptation. Similarly, if a woman responds to a man's sneeze, an old woman is answered verbally, but a young woman is answered silently in the heart.
This mirrors the rules for returning salam to women.
4
Compare with salam rules
The text explicitly states 'The ruling in this is like the ruling in greeting (salam).' This indicates that the same age-based distinction applies: respond verbally to an old woman, silently to a young woman.
The analogy (qiyas) is based on the shared cause of avoiding fitna.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشميت العاطس إذا كان خارج الصلاة السنة في حق العاطس أن يقول الحمد لله رب العالمين أو على كل حال، ولمن حضر أن يقول يرحمك الله فيرد عليه العاطس فيقول يغفر الله لك أو يهديك. وإذا عطست المرأة فلا بأس بتشميتها إلا أن تكون شابة، وإذا عطس الرجل فشمتته المرأة، فإن كانت عجوزاً يرد عليها، وإن كانت شابة يرد في قلبه والجواب في هذا كالجواب في السلام.
Sneezing etiquette: When outside prayer, it is sunnah for the sneezer to say 'Alhamdulillahi rabbil 'alameen' or 'on every condition', and for those present to say 'Yarhamukallah', then the sneezer responds 'Yaghfirullahu lak' or 'Yahdeek'. If a woman sneezes, it is permissible to respond to her unless she is young. If a man sneezes and a woman responds, if she is old he responds verbally, if she is young he responds in his heart. The ruling in this is like the ruling in greeting (salam).
Source pages p. 381

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on the etiquette of sneezing (tashmit al-'atis). It outlines the sunnah acts: the sneezer praises Allah, the hearer invokes mercy, and the sneezer prays for forgiveness or guidance. Specific rules apply when a woman sneezes: it is permissible to respond unless she is young and likely to cause fitna. If a woman responds to a man's sneeze, an old woman may be answered verbally, but a young woman should be answered silently in the heart, analogous to the rules of returning salam. This reflects the Hanafi concern for avoiding temptation.

Key Terms
تشميت العاطس (tashmit al-'atis): The act of responding to a sneeze with the supplication 'yarhamukallah'.
يرحمك الله (yarhamukallah): Supplication meaning 'May Allah have mercy on you' said to the sneezer.
شابة (shabbah): A young woman who may be a source of temptation; the age is relative but generally refers to a woman of marriageable age.

Ruling on Placing an Iron Collar on a Slave (al-Rayah)
Ruling with proof: prohibition of iron collar on slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on placing an iron collar (al-rayah) on a slave's neck, identify the proofs from hadith and qiyas, and distinguish it from permissible forms of discipline.

Core Idea
Placing a nailed collar that restricts movement is haram—it mirrors cruel punishment of disbelievers and is a forbidden innovation.

This lesson examines a specific practice from early Islamic contexts: putting an iron collar on a slave as a mark of punishment. The Hanafi school unequivocally declares it haram, drawing on both the general prohibition of innovation and an analogy to the forbidden act of burning with fire. You will learn the precise description of the act and the legal reasoning that supports this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its description
The act is placing a 'rayah' (iron collar) around the slave's neck, nailed to prevent head movement, typical of oppressors.
The collar is specifically described as 'مسمراً بمسمار عظيم' (nailed with a large nail) that prevents turning the head.
2
State the Hanafi ruling and its level
The ruling is haram (prohibited) based on the text and commentary.
The matn says 'لا يجوز' (not permissible), and the commentator explicitly says 'وهو حرام' (it is haram).
3
Analyze the dalil from hadith
The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Every newly invented matter is an innovation, every innovation is misguidance, and every misguidance is in the Fire.' This practice is a blameworthy innovation because it is a new method of punishment not sanctioned by Shariah.
The hadith is used to declare the act bid'ah (innovation) which is condemned.
4
Explain the qiyas (analogy) to burning
The act is analogized (qiyas) to burning with fire as punishment, which is haram because only Allah punishes with fire. The common illa (effective cause) is 'excessive cruel punishment not sanctioned by Shariah'.
The qiyas is from the general rule that punishments not authorized by Shariah are impermissible.
5
Note practical considerations for fatwa
The ruling is mufta bihi (operative) and absolute; other schools may permit if not excessive, but the Hanafi position is clear prohibition.
Cross-madhhab: other schools (e.g., Maliki) may allow a non-restraining mark, but the Hanafi ruling on this specific restrained collar is haram.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( وجعل الراية في عنق العبد أي لا يجوز ذلك. قال الشارح: وصورته أن يجعل في عنقه طوقاً مسمراً بمسمار عظيم يمنعه أن يحول رأسه وهو معتاد بین الظلمة وهو حرام لأن عقوبة الكافر تحرم كالإحراق بالنار وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام كل محدث بدعة وكل بدعة ضلالة وكل ضلالة في النار)
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And making the collar on the slave's neck) meaning it is not permissible. The commentator said: Its description is that he places a collar around his neck nailed with a large nail that prevents him from turning his head, and it is common among oppressors, and it is haram because punishing the disbeliever is forbidden like burning with fire. And he (peace be upon him) said: Every newly invented matter is an innovation, every innovation is misguidance, and every misguidance is in the Fire.
Source pages p. 381

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof (dalil) from the sharh. The matn states that making a 'rayah' (a collar or mark) on a slave's neck is not permissible. The commentator (sharih) explains this refers to placing an iron collar that prevents head movement, a practice of tyrants. The ruling is haram, analogized to burning with fire which is forbidden as punishment. The proof is the hadith condemning all innovations, equating this practice to a blameworthy innovation. The hanafi position is clear prohibition.

Key Terms
الراية (al-rayah): An iron collar placed around the neck as a mark of absconding or punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) Because it is not mentioned in the Quran

Key Takeaway
Placing a restraining iron collar on a slave is haram due to its cruelty and innovation, analogized to burning with fire.

Ruling on Slave Collars and Shackling in Hanafi Fiqh
Further rulings on collars and shackling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on shackling a slave and identify the conditions that make it permissible or disliked.

Core Idea
Collars and shackling are permissible when needed to prevent absconding but were disliked when absconding was rare.

This passage from Baḥr al-Rāʾiq presents rulings on two related practices: placing a collar on a slave and shackling his hands. The author draws on al-Nihāyah and al-Sirājiyyah to show how the ruling shifts based on social context and individual circumstances. The phrase 'ḥallu qaydihi' (undoing his shackle) is used idiomatically to mean the opposite—shackling is permitted. Understanding this ruling requires attention to the condition of prevalent absconding and the intention behind the act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon (placing a collar, shackling hands) and the baseline hukm (disliked vs. permissible).
The collar was disliked in earlier times due to rarity of absconding; now permissible.
2
Note the contextual shift
The ruling changed because the underlying custom ('urf) changed. Frequent absconding makes the measure necessary.
Especially among Indians (al-Hunūd) in the author's time.
3
Identify the condition for permissibility
Shackling is permissible when there is fear of the slave absconding or for reform (following the sunnah of Muslims toward the wicked).
Also allowed when a judge fears for his safety.
4
Recognize the contranym in 'ḥallu qaydihi'
The literal meaning 'undoing his shackle' is used figuratively to mean 'shackling is permitted'—a case of linguistic license.
Context clarifies the intended ruling.
5
Understand the sunnah dimension
Shackling a wicked slave for reform is described as 'the practice (sunnah) of Muslims', indicating it is commendable when done with proper intent.
The judge who administers justice is rewarded even if he shackles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي النهاية : الراية علامة أنه آبق ولا بأس به في زماننا الغلبة الإباق خصوصاً في الهنود وكان في زمانهم مكروهاً لقلة الإباق ا هـ . وفي السراجية : ويكره أن يغل يديه ولو كان الرجل يقوم ويوزع المظالم من الإمام بالعدل والأنصاف كان مأجوراً، وإن خاف الرجل على نفسه لا بأس به. قال رحمه الله : (وحل قيده) يعني جاز قيد العبد احترازاً من الإباق والتمرد وهو سنة المسلمين في الفساق
And in al-Nihayah: The collar is a sign that he is an absconder, and there is no harm in it in our time because of the prevalence of absconding, especially among the Indians. In their time it was disliked due to the rarity of absconding. End quote. And in al-Sirajiyyah: It is disliked to shackle his hands, and if a man performs and distributes justice from the ruler with fairness and equity, he is rewarded. If a man fears for himself, there is no harm. He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And undoing his shackle) meaning it is permissible to shackle the slave to prevent absconding and rebellion, and it is the practice of Muslims towards the wicked.
Source pages p. 381

Commentary
This passage presents additional rulings on slave collars and shackling. From al-Nihayah: although placing a collar was previously disliked due to rare absconding, it is now permissible when absconding is widespread (especially in India). From al-Sirajiyyah: shackling hands is generally disliked, but a man who distributes justice is rewarded, and if he fears for his safety, shackling is allowed. Then the matn states the ruling on 'undoing his shackle' (حل قيده) meaning it is permissible to shackle a slave to prevent escape and rebellion, and this is the sunnah of Muslims towards the wicked. Note that 'undoing' is interpreted as 'shackling' (i.e., the opposite meaning by way of license). The ruling is that shackling is permissible when needed, and it is considered a sunnah practice for dealing with wrongdoers.

Key Terms
الراية (al-rāyah): A collar placed on a slave's neck to mark him as an absconder.
حل قيده (ḥallu qaydihi): Literally 'undoing his shackle'; here interpreted as permissibility of shackling.
الإباق (al-ibāq): Absconding of a slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because slaves are more rebellious
B) Because absconding has become prevalent
C) Because the Prophet permitted it
D) Because it is a sign of ownership

Key Takeaway
Shackling and collars are permissible in the Hanafi school when absconding is prevalent or for reform, but were disliked when such problems were rare.

Enema and Medical Treatment: Permissibility and Conditions
Ruling with proof on enema and medical treatment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on enema for treatment and explain the condition regarding belief in the source of cure.

Core Idea
Medical treatment is permissible if one believes cure comes from Allah; believing medicine cures independently is blameworthy.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the permissibility of using an enema (huqnah) for medical treatment. The author cites hadiths encouraging seeking treatment and addresses objections from those who consider treatment contrary to tawakkul. The key condition is that one's belief must be that Allah alone is the healer, not the medicine itself. The discussion extends to ruqyah (incantations) and the prohibition of pre-Islamic forms.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is using an enema for medical treatment. According to the matn, it is permissible (mubah).
The ruling is explicitly stated as permissible (tajuz).
2
Locate the dalil
The author supports permissibility with the hadith: 'For every disease there is a cure, and when you hit upon the cure, it is cured by Allah's permission.' This indicates causation and encourages seeking treatment.
The hadith is cited from Muslim and Ahmad.
3
Address the counter-evidence
Some scholars disliked treatment based on the hadith about those who enter Paradise without reckoning because they do not seek ruqyah or cauterize. The Hanafi response is that this hadith describes a high level of tawakkul, not a prohibition.
The commentary emphasizes that the two hadiths are not contradictory.
4
State the condition for permissibility
The patient must believe that cure comes from Allah, not that the medicine itself cures. If one believes the medicine cures independently, it becomes blameworthy (makruh).
The text says: 'No sin on one who seeks treatment if he believes cure is from Allah.'
5
Apply to ruqyah
Ruqyah with Quran and permissible supplications is permissible as the Prophet practiced it. The prohibition in other hadiths refers to pre-Islamic ruqyah involving shirk.
The hadith 'Ruqyah, amulets, and tiwadah are shirk' is interpreted accordingly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (والحقنة) يعني تجوز للتداوي وجاز أن يظهر إلى ذلك الموضع للضرورة لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم «لكل داء دواء وإذا أصبت دواه لداء بإذن الله تعالى رواه مسلم وأحمد. وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام لكل داء دواء إلا الهرم فإنه دواء له وراه الترمذي وصححه. ومن الناس من كره التداوي لما روى ابن عباس أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال يدخل من أمتي سبعون ألفاً الجنة بغير حساب وهم الذي لا يسترقون ولا يتطيرون ولا يكتوون وعلى ربهم يتوكلون رواه البخاري. ولنا ما قدمنا من الأحاديث. ولا جناح على من يتداوى إذا كان يعتقد أن الشفاء من الله تعالى، وما ورد من النهي عن الدواء إذا كان يعتقد أن الشفاء الدواء وهو محل الكراهة . قال الشارح ونحن نقول : لا يجوز لمثل هذا التداوي، ولا فرق بين الرجل المرأة. وإنما يجوز التداوي بالأشياء الطاهرة ولا يجوز بالنجس كالخمر وغيره كما قدمنا، والتداوي لا يمنع التوكل ولا بأس بالرقيا لأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام كان يفعله، وما روي من النهي كان محمولاً على رقي الجاهلية لأنهم كانوا يرقون بألفاظ كفر، وما رواه ابن مسعود أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام قال الرقي والتمائم والتؤدة شرك محمول على ما ذكرنا . قال الأصمعي : التؤدة ضرب من السحر يحبب المرأة إلى زوجها. وعن عائشة رضي الله تعالى عنها كان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم إذا مرض أحد من أهله تفث عليه بالمعوذتين، فلما مرض المرض الذي مات فيه جعلت أنفث عليه وأمس جسده بيده لأن أبرك من يدي.
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And the enema) meaning it is permissible for treatment, and it is permissible to expose that area out of necessity, due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'For every disease there is a cure, and when you hit upon the cure for the disease, it is cured by Allah's permission' narrated by Muslim and Ahmad. And he (peace be upon him) said: 'For every disease there is a cure except old age, for it has no cure' narrated by Tirmidhi and authenticated. Some people disliked medical treatment because of what Ibn Abbas narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Seventy thousand of my ummah will enter Paradise without reckoning, those who do not seek ruqyah, do not believe in omens, do not cauterize, and rely on their Lord' narrated by Bukhari. In our support we have the previous hadith. There is no sin on one who seeks treatment if he believes that cure is from Allah Almighty. The prohibition reported against medicine is when one believes that the medicine itself cures, and that is the place of dislike. The commentator said: And we say: It is not permissible for such a person to seek treatment, and there is no difference between man and woman. Treatment is only permissible with pure things, not with impurities like wine and others as we have mentioned. Treatment does not negate tawakkul. There is no harm in ruqyah because the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to do it. What is reported of prohibition is interpreted as the ruqyah of the Jahiliyyah because they used to recite words of kufr. And what Ibn Mas'ud narrated that he (peace be upon him) said: 'Ruqyah, amulets, and tiwadah are shirk' is interpreted accordingly. Al-Asma'i said: Tiwadah is a type of magic that makes a woman beloved to her husband. And from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her): When anyone of his family fell ill, the Prophet (peace be upon him) would blow over him with the Mu'awwidhatayn. When he fell ill with his fatal illness, I began to blow over him and wipe his body with my hand because it was more blessed than my hand.
Source pages p. 381

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof on the permissibility of enema (huqnah) for medical treatment. The matn states it is permissible, and the sharh provides proofs from hadith: 'For every disease there is a cure' and the exception of old age. Some scholars disliked treatment based on the hadith about those who do not seek treatment, but the majority (Hanafi) rely on the first hadiths. The condition is that the patient believes cure comes from Allah, not that the medicine itself cures. If one believes the medicine cures independently, it is blameworthy. Treatment must use pure substances; impure ones like wine are not allowed. The discussion extends to ruqyah (incantation): it is permissible as the Prophet practiced it; prohibition refers to pre-Islamic forms involving kufr. The story of Aisha confirms the Prophet's practice of ruqyah with the Mu'awwidhatayn.

Key Terms
الحقنة (al-huqnah): An enema, the injection of fluid into the rectum for medical purposes.
الرقيا (al-ruqyah): Recitation of Quranic verses or permissible supplications for healing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition is medical treatment blameworthy according to the text?
A) When the patient is poor
B) When the treatment uses impure substances
C) When the patient believes the medicine itself cures
D) When the patient does not also make du'a

Key Takeaway
Medical treatment is permissible in Hanafi fiqh as a means, provided one's belief in cure is from Allah and the substances used are pure.

Guardian's Right to Take from Minor's Property for Maintenance
Ruling on guardian taking minor's property for maintenance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the guardian taking from a minor's property for maintenance, specify the permissible amount, and explain the effect of customary practice (urf) on the timing of the stipend.

Core Idea
A guardian may take only the minor's sufficiency from his property, not more.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies when and how much a guardian may take from a minor's property for maintenance. It addresses specific guardians (paternal uncle, mother, finder) and ties the customary timing of the stipend to the collection of kharaj. The ruling ensures the minor's welfare while preventing exploitation by the guardian.

Guided Path
1
Identify the guardian and subject
The text specifies the guardian: paternal uncle, mother, or finder of a foundling, provided they have custody (fi hijrihim). The subject is the minor's property.
Guardians other than these (e.g., father) are not mentioned here; their ruling may differ.
2
Determine the permissible amount
The guardian may take only the amount of sufficiency (kifayah) and family expenses ('aylah) for the minor and his dependents. Taking more is prohibited.
The amount is determined by need, not by guardian's discretion.
3
Analyze the customary practice ('urf)
The text describes a custom: the stipend is given at the beginning of the year because kharaj (land tax) was collected at the beginning. However, in the author's time, kharaj is collected at the end of the year, so the correct view is that the stipend is for the past year (i.e., given after the year).
This demonstrates how custom (urf) can influence legal practice as long as it does not contradict a text.
4
Handle dismissal mid-year
If the guardian takes the stipend at the beginning of the year but is dismissed before the year ends, he must return the portion of the year remaining. This is based on the same principle as the wife's stipend, with a similar difference of opinion.
The mention of 'difference regarding the wife' refers to a known Hanafi internal ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
للصغير منه وبيعه للعم والأم والملتقط لو في حجرهم. يأخذ منه مقدار كفايته وعيلته وليس له أن يأخذ أزيد من ذلك. وقد جرى الرسم بالإعطاء في أول السنة لأن الخراج كان يؤخذ في أول السنة وهو يعطي منه، وفي زماننا يؤخذ الخراج في آخر السنة والمأخوذ عن السنة الماضية في الصحيح وعليه الفتوى. ولو أخذ الرزق في أول السنة ثم عزل قبل مضي السنة رد ما بقي من السنة، وقيل هو على الخلاف في الزوجة على ما بينا ا هـ .
For the minor, and his sale for the paternal uncle, the mother, and the finder if they are in their care. He takes from it the amount of his sufficiency and his family's expenses, and he may not take more than that. The custom has applied of giving at the beginning of the year because the kharaj was taken at the beginning of the year and he gives from it, and in our time the kharaj is taken at the end of the year, and what is taken for the past year is the correct view and upon it is the fatwa. If he took the stipend at the beginning of the year then was dismissed before the year passed, he returns what remains of the year, and it is said it is based on the difference regarding the wife as we explained. End.
Source pages p. 383

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the ruling on the guardian (paternal uncle, mother, or finder of a foundling) taking from the minor's property for his maintenance. The ruling states that he may take only the amount sufficient for his and his dependents' needs, not more. The text then discusses the customary practice of giving the stipend at the beginning of the year, linked to the timing of kharaj collection. In their time, kharaj was collected at the start of the year, so the stipend was given then. In the author's time, kharaj was collected at the end of the year, so the accepted view is that the stipend is for the past year, and this is the basis for fatwa. If the guardian takes the stipend at the beginning and is dismissed before the year ends, he must return the proportion for the remaining period. There is a difference of opinion similar to that regarding the wife.

Key Terms
الكفاية والعيلة (al-kifayah wa al-'aylah): Sufficiency and family expenses: the necessary maintenance for the minor and his dependents.
الخراج (al-kharaj): Land tax; the timing of its collection influenced the customary practice of giving stipends.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a guardian takes more than the minor's necessary maintenance from his property?
A) It is permissible if the guardian is the father.
B) It is not allowed; he may only take the amount of sufficiency.
C) It is permissible if the minor is rich.
D) It is obligatory to take the maximum.

Key Takeaway
A guardian may take from a minor's property only what is needed for the minor's maintenance, and the timing of this stipend follows established custom as long as it does not conflict with Shariah.

Travel of Female Slave and Umm Walad Without Mahram
Ruling on travel of female slave without mahram with temporal qualification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on travel of female slaves without a mahram, identify its basis by analogy, and explain the temporal change in its application.

Core Idea
Female slaves were originally allowed to travel without mahram, but later prohibited due to corruption.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling on travel for female slaves and umm walad without a mahram. The text from al-Bahr al-Raiq bases the permissibility on the slave's status being akin to a mahram for all men. However, later authorities qualified this ruling based on the prevalence of moral corruption, shifting the operative fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its original ruling
The act is travel of a female slave or umm walad without a mahram. The original ruling is permissibility (mubah).
This is the rule as per the explicit text.
2
Understand the legal basis (talil)
The female slave is in the position of a mahram for all men regarding looking and touching. This analogy makes a mahram unnecessary for her travel.
The equal status in looking/touching is the effective cause (illa).
3
Apply the analogy to similar categories
The ruling extends to umm walad, mukatabah, mudabbirah, and (according to Abu Hanifa) a partially freed woman, due to the presence of slavery in them.
All these categories share the illa of being a slave.
4
Recognize the temporal qualification
Al-Kafi and Shaykh al-Islam state that the ruling applied only when righteousness prevailed. In later times of corruption, travel without mahram is not permissible.
This is a change in the hukm based on changing circumstances.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The operative ruling for fatwa today is the prohibition, as corruption is widespread.
This is the position of the later Hanafi authorities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : وسفر الأمة وأم الولد بلا محرم) يعني يجوز لهما السفر بغير محرم لأن الأمة بمنزلة المحرم لسائر الرجال فيما يرجع إلى النظر والمس على ما بينا، وأم الولد والمكاتبة والمدبرة كالأمة لقيام الرق فيهن وكذا معتقة البعض عند الإمام لأنها كالمكاتبة عنده . وفي الكافي قالوا: هذا في زمانهم لغلبة أهل الصلاح، أما في زماننا فلا يجوز لغلبة أهل الفساد ومثله في النهاية معزياً إلى شيخ الإسلام.
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'And travel of the female slave and umm walad without a mahram' — meaning it is permissible for both of them to travel without a mahram because the female slave is in the position of a mahram for all men with regard to looking and touching as we explained, and the umm walad, the mukatabah, and the mudabbirah are like the female slave due to the presence of slavery in them, and likewise a partially freed woman according to Imam Abu Hanifa because she is like a mukatabah according to him. In al-Kafi they said: This was in their time due to the prevalence of righteous people; as for our time, it is not permissible due to the prevalence of corrupt people, and similar is in al-Nihayah attributed to Shaykh al-Islam.
Source pages p. 383

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses the permissibility of travel without a mahram for a female slave and umm walad. The ruling states that it is permissible because the female slave is akin to a mahram with respect to looking and touching for all men, as she is not a free woman. The same applies to the umm walad, mukatabah, mudabbirah, and a partially freed woman according to Abu Hanifa. However, al-Kafi notes that this ruling applied in their time when righteousness prevailed; in later times, due to moral corruption, it is no longer permissible. This opinion is attributed to Shaykh al-Islam.

Key Terms
الأمة (al-ammah): Female slave; she is considered like a mahram in terms of looking and touching.
أم الولد (umm al-walad): A slave woman who has borne a child to her master; she is like a female slave in this ruling.
محرم (mahram): A permanently unmarriageable relative; the text says the female slave is 'in the position of a mahram' for all men.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does al-Kafi say the ruling on travel without mahram for female slaves changed in later times?
A) Because female slaves became more numerous.
B) Due to the prevalence of corrupt people.
C) Because of a change in the legal texts.
D) Because the Prophet's hadith was abrogated.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on female slave travel without mahram changed from permissible to impermissible based on societal corruption, showing the importance of temporal context.

The Definition and Conditions of Al-Mawat
Defining al-mawat and its three conditions with the hadith proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for land to be classified as mawat and identify the hadith proof that allows ownership upon revival.

Core Idea
Mawat land must be uncultivable due to water deficiency or excess, non-owned, and distant from inhabited areas.

This lesson opens the chapter on reviving dead lands (ihya al-mawat) by precisely defining what qualifies as 'dead land' (al-mawat). The definition is not arbitrary: it rests on a hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and sets the boundaries for when a person can acquire ownership by reviving land. Understanding these three conditions is essential before moving to the rules of revival.

Guided Path
1
Extract the three conditions from the matn
Identify in the author's definition the three requirements: difficulty of cultivation due to water, non-ownership, and distance from inhabited area.
The matn states: 'هي أرض تعذر زراعتها لانقطاع الماء عنها أو لغلبته عليها غير مملوكة بعيدة من العامر'
2
Understand the rationale for each condition
The commentator explains why each element is necessary; e.g., 'land' is a genus, 'difficult cultivation' excludes cultivable land, etc.
Each phrase in the definition excludes something: 'تعذر' excludes cultivable, 'غير مملوكة' excludes owned, 'بعيدة' excludes near land.
3
Locate the hadith proof
The Prophet's statement 'Whoever revives a dead land, it is for him' is the primary evidence for ownership through revival.
The hadith is ahad in transmission but clear in meaning (qati al-dalala).
4
Note the exception for land with an unknown owner
In dar al-Islam, if the owner is unknown, the land is treated as a lost item (luqata), not as mawat, because ownership is presumed to persist.
The imam deals with such land like a lost item; if the owner appears later, he can reclaim it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب إحياء الموات
هي أرض تعذر زراعتها لانقطاع الماء عنها أو لغلبته عليها غير مملوكة بعيدة من العامر
مناسبة هذا الكتاب بكتاب الكراهية يجوز أن يكون من حيث إن هذا الكتاب مشتمل على ما يكره وما لا يكره ويكفي فيها أدنى المناسبة والكلام هنا في وجوه: الأول في معناه لغة. والثاني في معناه شرعاً والثالث في شرطه والرابع في سببه. والخامس في دليله. والسادس في حكمه. أما دليله فقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام" من أحياء أرضاً ميتة فهي له» وأما معناه لغة قال في الصحاح : والموات بالفتح ما لا روح فيه، والموات أيضاً الأرض التي لا مالك لها من الآدميين. وفي القاموس الموات كغراب وسحاب ما لا روح فيه والأرض لا ملك لها من الآدميين ا.هـ. وشرعاً ما سيأتي في عبارة المؤلف وسبب المشروعية تعلق البناء المقرر على الوجه الأكمل وشرطه سيأتي في حكم تملك المحيي ما أحياه. قال رحمه الله : (هي أرض تعذر زراعتها لانقطاع الماء عنها أو لغلبته عليها غير مملوكة بعيدة من العامر) فقوله أرض بمنزلة الجنس يشمل ما تعذر وغيره، وقوله تعذر» أخرج غيره فلا يكون مواتاً، وقوله لانقطاع الماء عنها أو لغلبته عليها بيان السبب التعذر ، وقوله «غير مملوكة» أخرج ما كان كذلك وهو مملوك فلا يكون مواتاً، وقوله بعيدة عن العامر» أخرج القريبة فلا تكون مواتاً. قال الشارح وأما تفسير لموات الأرض. وإنما سميت مواتاً إذا كانت بهذه الصفة لبطلان الانتفاع بها تشبيهاً بالميت قال الشارح : وهذا تفسير الحياة فظاهر. قال في العناية : والإحياء شرعاً أن يكرب الأرض ويسقيها فإن كربها ولم يسقها أو سقاها ولم يكربها فليس بإحياء، وفي الكافي : لو فعل أحدهما يكون إحياء وعن أبي يوسف: الإحياء البناء والغراس أو الكرب أو السقي. وعن محمد الكرب الإحياء وفي الغياثية عن محمد: الكرب ليس بإحياء إلا أن يبذرها وعن شمس الأئمة : الأحياء أن يجعلها صالحة للزارعة . وفي الخانية : لو بنى في بعض أرض الموات أو زرع فيها كان ذلك إحياء لذلك البعض دون غيره إلا أن يكون ما عمر أكثر من النصف في قول أبي يوسف. وقال محمد: إذا كان الموات في وسط الأحياء يكون إحياء للكل ا هـ . والإحياء لغة الإنبات سواء كان بفعل فاعل من شراء وغير ذلك، ولا يقال لماذا عرف المؤلف الموات دون الإحياء والمناسب أن يعرفهما معاً لأنا نقول : أراد بيان الأكمل وإنما ترك تعريف الإحياء. قال الشارح: لأنه ظاهر. وقوله «غيره مملوكه» يعني في دار الإسلام لأن الميت الإطلاق ينصرف إلى الكامل وكماله بأن لا يكون مملوكاً لأحد لأنها إذا كانت مملوكة لمسلم أو ذمي كان ملكه باقياً لعدم ما يزيله فلا يكون مواتاً، فإذا عرف المالك فهي له وإن لم يعرف كانت لقطة يتصرف فيها الإمام كما يتصرف في اللقطة، ولو ظهر لها مالك بعد ذلك أخذها وضمن من زرعها إن نقصت بالزراعة وإلا فلا شيء عليه، وقول القدوري فما كان منها عادياً مراده بالعادي ما قدم خرابه كأنه منسوب إلى عاد الخراب عهدهم. وجعل المملوك في دار الإسلام إذا لم يعرف له مالك من الموات لأن حكمه كالموات لأنه لا يعرف له مالك بعينه وليس هو مواتاً حقيقة على ما بينا. وقوله «بعيدة عن العامر» هو قول أبي يوسف والبعيدة أن تكون بحيث لو وقف إنسان في أقصى العامر وصاح بأعلى صوته لم يسمع منه فهو موات، وإن كان يسمع فليس بموات لأنه أهل العامر يحتاجون إليه لرعي مواشيهم وطرح حصائدهم فلم یکن انتفاعهم به منقطعاً. وعند محمد يعتبر حقيقة الانتفاع حتى لا يجوز إحياء ما ينتفع به أهل القرية وإن كان بعيداً، ويجوز إحياء ما لا ينتفعون به وإن كان قريباً، وشمس الأئمة اعتمد قول أبي يوسف
Book of Reviving Dead Lands. It is land whose cultivation is difficult due to lack of water or its overwhelming presence, not owned, distant from inhabited area. The connection of this book to the book of dislike [al-karahiyya] is possible in that this book contains what is disliked and what is not disliked, and minimal appropriateness suffices. The discussion here is in aspects: first: its linguistic meaning, second: its legal meaning, third: its condition, fourth: its cause, fifth: its proof, sixth: its ruling. As for its proof, his statement, peace be upon him: 'Whoever revives a dead land, it is for him.' As for its linguistic meaning, it is said in al-Sihah: al-mawat (with fatha) is that which has no soul, and al-mawat also is land that has no owner from humans. In al-Qamus: al-mawat (like ghurab and sahab) is that which has no soul, and land with no owner from humans. End quote. And legally, it will come in the author's phrase. The reason for legislation is the attachment of established construction in the most complete manner, and its condition will come in the ruling of the reviver's ownership of what he revived. He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: (It is land whose cultivation is difficult due to lack of water or its overwhelming presence, not owned, distant from inhabited area.) So his saying 'land' is like a genus encompassing what is difficult and otherwise. His saying 'becomes difficult' excludes other than it, so it is not mawat. His saying 'due to lack of water or its overwhelming presence' is an explanation of the cause of difficulty. His saying 'not owned' excludes what is owned, so it is not mawat. His saying 'distant from inhabited area' excludes the near, so it is not mawat. The commentator said: As for the interpretation of mawat land, it is only called mawat if it has this description due to the nullification of benefit from it, by analogy with the dead. The commentator said: This is an apparent interpretation of life. It is said in al-Inaya: Revival legally is that one turns the soil and waters it. If he turns the soil but does not water it, or waters it but does not turn it, it is not revival. In al-Kafi: If he does one of them, it is revival. From Abu Yusuf: Revival is building, planting, turning soil, or watering. From Muhammad: Turning soil is revival. In al-Ghiyathiyya from Muhammad: Turning soil is not revival unless he sows it. From Shams al-A'imma: Revival is making it suitable for cultivation. In al-Khaniyya: If he builds in part of dead land or sows in it, that is revival for that part only, unless what he developed is more than half according to Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said: If the dead land is in the middle of inhabited land, it is revival for all. End quote. Linguistically, revival means causing growth, whether by an act of an agent through purchase or otherwise. It is not said why the author defined mawat and not revival, when it would be appropriate to define both together. We say: He intended to explain the complete description, and he deliberately left the definition of revival. The commentator said: because it is apparent. His saying 'other than owned' means in the abode of Islam because the absolute dead [land] refers to the complete, and its completeness is that it is not owned by anyone because if it is owned by a Muslim or a dhimmi, his ownership remains for lack of what removes it, so it is not mawat. If the owner is known, it is his; if unknown, it is a luqata (lost item) with which the imam deals as he deals with luqata. If an owner appears later, he takes it and holds liable the one who cultivated it if it decreased due to cultivation; otherwise nothing is upon him. The saying of al-Quduri: 'What is ancient' means what has long been in ruin, as if attributed to the people of 'Ad. And the owned in the abode of Islam if no owner is known is considered mawat because its ruling is like mawat since no specific owner is known, though it is not really mawat as we explained. His saying 'distant from inhabited area' is the saying of Abu Yusuf: distant is such that if a person stands at the farthest part of the inhabited area and shouts at the top of his voice, it is not heard; then it is mawat. If it is heard, it is not mawat because the inhabitants of the inhabited area need it for grazing their livestock and throwing their harvests, so their benefit from it is not cut off. According to Muhammad, actual benefit is considered: it is not permissible to revive what the village people benefit from even if distant, and it is permissible to revive what they do not benefit from even if near. Shams al-A'imma relied on Abu Yusuf's saying.
Source pages p. 385

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the chapter on reviving dead lands (Ihya al-Mawat) from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The author first defines al-mawat as land whose cultivation is impossible due to lack of water or its overwhelming presence, which is not owned by anyone, and is distant from inhabited areas. The commentator expands on each condition: 'land' is a genus; 'difficult cultivation' excludes cultivable land; the reasons for difficulty are explained; 'not owned' excludes land that belongs to someone; 'distant from an inhabited area' excludes land near villages or towns. The proof for the ruling is the hadith 'Whoever revives a dead land, it is for him.' The linguistic meaning of mawat is also given from lexicons. Then the commentator discusses the legal definition of 'revival' (ihya) according to different Hanafi authorities: some require both turning the soil and watering; others consider one sufficient; Abu Yusuf includes building and planting; Muhammad requires turning the soil; another view requires sowing. There is also a discussion on the distance criterion: according to Abu Yusuf, if a shout from the edge of the inhabited area cannot be heard, the land is mawat; according to Muhammad, the key is actual benefit by the villagers. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) according to Shams al-A'imma is that of Abu Yusuf. The passage also clarifies that land with an unknown owner in dar al-Islam is treated as a lost item (luqata), not as mawat, and the imam deals with it accordingly. This lesson establishes the foundational definition and conditions for the chapter.

Key Terms
الموات (al-mawāt): Land that is difficult to cultivate due to lack of water or its overwhelming presence, not owned by anyone, and distant from inhabited areas.
العامر (al-'āmir): Inhabited land, such as villages or towns, from which the distance of mawat is measured.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a condition for land to be considered mawat?
A) It must be owned by a Muslim.
B) It must be near an inhabited area.
C) It must be non-owned and distant from inhabited areas.
D) It must have a known owner.

Key Takeaway
The legal classification of land as mawat rests on three precise conditions: water-related difficulty, non-ownership, and distance from inhabited areas; only such land can be revived and owned through ihya.
