The Definition of Ihya (Revival) and the Distance Criterion
Intra-Hanafi discussion on the definition of ihya and the distance condition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the various Hanafi opinions on what constitutes ihya of dead land and apply the relied-upon position on the distance criterion.

Core Idea
Ihya of mawat land is achieved by making it cultivable; the distance from inhabited areas is determined by audibility of a shout (Abu Yusuf's view, relied upon).

After defining mawat, the passage delves into what exactly constitutes 'revival' (ihya) and how to measure the required distance from inhabited areas. The Hanafi school has multiple opinions on these matters, reflecting different approaches to the hadith 'Whoever revives a dead land, it is for him.' This lesson clarifies the key views and the mufta bihi positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main opinions on ihya
List the definitions from al-Inaya, al-Kafi, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Shams al-A'imma.
al-Inaya requires both turning soil and watering; al-Kafi says either suffices; Abu Yusuf includes building and planting; Muhammad emphasizes turning soil; Shams al-A'imma synthesizes as making land cultivable.
2
Understand the ruling on partial revival
Discuss the difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on reviving part of a plot.
Abu Yusuf: if revived part > half, he owns the whole? No: he owns only the part revived unless the rest is surrounded? Actually the text says: if he builds in part, he owns that part; if he develops more than half, he owns all according to Abu Yusuf? The text says: ' إلا أن يكون ما عمر أكثر من النصف في قول أبي يوسف' meaning he owns the whole if developed more than half? Actually it says: 'يكون إحياء لذلك البعض دون غيره إلا أن يكون ما عمر أكثر من النصف في قول أبي يوسف' – he owns that part only unless the developed part is more than half; then he owns the whole? The wording is ambiguous; but the point is disagreement.
3
Examine the distance criterion
Understand Abu Yusuf's audibility test and Muhammad's actual-benefit test.
Abu Yusuf: if a shout from the edge of the village is not heard, the land is mawat. Muhammad: if villagers actually benefit from the land (e.g., grazing), it is not mawat even if far.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
Note that Shams al-A'imma relied on Abu Yusuf's view on distance.
This indicates the preferred position for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب إحياء الموات
هي أرض تعذر زراعتها لانقطاع الماء عنها أو لغلبته عليها غير مملوكة بعيدة من العامر
مناسبة هذا الكتاب بكتاب الكراهية يجوز أن يكون من حيث إن هذا الكتاب مشتمل على ما يكره وما لا يكره ويكفي فيها أدنى المناسبة والكلام هنا في وجوه: الأول في معناه لغة. والثاني في معناه شرعاً والثالث في شرطه والرابع في سببه. والخامس في دليله. والسادس في حكمه. أما دليله فقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام" من أحياء أرضاً ميتة فهي له» وأما معناه لغة قال في الصحاح : والموات بالفتح ما لا روح فيه، والموات أيضاً الأرض التي لا مالك لها من الآدميين. وفي القاموس الموات كغراب وسحاب ما لا روح فيه والأرض لا ملك لها من الآدميين ا.هـ. وشرعاً ما سيأتي في عبارة المؤلف وسبب المشروعية تعلق البناء المقرر على الوجه الأكمل وشرطه سيأتي في حكم تملك المحيي ما أحياه. قال رحمه الله : (هي أرض تعذر زراعتها لانقطاع الماء عنها أو لغلبته عليها غير مملوكة بعيدة من العامر) فقوله أرض بمنزلة الجنس يشمل ما تعذر وغيره، وقوله تعذر» أخرج غيره فلا يكون مواتاً، وقوله لانقطاع الماء عنها أو لغلبته عليها بيان السبب التعذر ، وقوله «غير مملوكة» أخرج ما كان كذلك وهو مملوك فلا يكون مواتاً، وقوله بعيدة عن العامر» أخرج القريبة فلا تكون مواتاً. قال الشارح وأما تفسير لموات الأرض. وإنما سميت مواتاً إذا كانت بهذه الصفة لبطلان الانتفاع بها تشبيهاً بالميت قال الشارح : وهذا تفسير الحياة فظاهر. قال في العناية : والإحياء شرعاً أن يكرب الأرض ويسقيها فإن كربها ولم يسقها أو سقاها ولم يكربها فليس بإحياء، وفي الكافي : لو فعل أحدهما يكون إحياء وعن أبي يوسف: الإحياء البناء والغراس أو الكرب أو السقي. وعن محمد الكرب الإحياء وفي الغياثية عن محمد: الكرب ليس بإحياء إلا أن يبذرها وعن شمس الأئمة : الأحياء أن يجعلها صالحة للزارعة . وفي الخانية : لو بنى في بعض أرض الموات أو زرع فيها كان ذلك إحياء لذلك البعض دون غيره إلا أن يكون ما عمر أكثر من النصف في قول أبي يوسف. وقال محمد: إذا كان الموات في وسط الأحياء يكون إحياء للكل ا هـ . والإحياء لغة الإنبات سواء كان بفعل فاعل من شراء وغير ذلك، ولا يقال لماذا عرف المؤلف الموات دون الإحياء والمناسب أن يعرفهما معاً لأنا نقول : أراد بيان الأكمل وإنما ترك تعريف الإحياء. قال الشارح: لأنه ظاهر. وقوله «غيره مملوكه» يعني في دار الإسلام لأن الميت الإطلاق ينصرف إلى الكامل وكماله بأن لا يكون مملوكاً لأحد لأنها إذا كانت مملوكة لمسلم أو ذمي كان ملكه باقياً لعدم ما يزيله فلا يكون مواتاً، فإذا عرف المالك فهي له وإن لم يعرف كانت لقطة يتصرف فيها الإمام كما يتصرف في اللقطة، ولو ظهر لها مالك بعد ذلك أخذها وضمن من زرعها إن نقصت بالزراعة وإلا فلا شيء عليه، وقول القدوري فما كان منها عادياً مراده بالعادي ما قدم خرابه كأنه منسوب إلى عاد الخراب عهدهم. وجعل المملوك في دار الإسلام إذا لم يعرف له مالك من الموات لأن حكمه كالموات لأنه لا يعرف له مالك بعينه وليس هو مواتاً حقيقة على ما بينا. وقوله «بعيدة عن العامر» هو قول أبي يوسف والبعيدة أن تكون بحيث لو وقف إنسان في أقصى العامر وصاح بأعلى صوته لم يسمع منه فهو موات، وإن كان يسمع فليس بموات لأنه أهل العامر يحتاجون إليه لرعي مواشيهم وطرح حصائدهم فلم یکن انتفاعهم به منقطعاً. وعند محمد يعتبر حقيقة الانتفاع حتى لا يجوز إحياء ما ينتفع به أهل القرية وإن كان بعيداً، ويجوز إحياء ما لا ينتفعون به وإن كان قريباً، وشمس الأئمة اعتمد قول أبي يوسف
Book of Reviving Dead Lands. It is land whose cultivation is difficult due to lack of water or its overwhelming presence, not owned, distant from inhabited area. The connection of this book to the book of dislike [al-karahiyya] is possible in that this book contains what is disliked and what is not disliked, and minimal appropriateness suffices. The discussion here is in aspects: first: its linguistic meaning, second: its legal meaning, third: its condition, fourth: its cause, fifth: its proof, sixth: its ruling. As for its proof, his statement, peace be upon him: 'Whoever revives a dead land, it is for him.' As for its linguistic meaning, it is said in al-Sihah: al-mawat (with fatha) is that which has no soul, and al-mawat also is land that has no owner from humans. In al-Qamus: al-mawat (like ghurab and sahab) is that which has no soul, and land with no owner from humans. End quote. And legally, it will come in the author's phrase. The reason for legislation is the attachment of established construction in the most complete manner, and its condition will come in the ruling of the reviver's ownership of what he revived. He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: (It is land whose cultivation is difficult due to lack of water or its overwhelming presence, not owned, distant from inhabited area.) So his saying 'land' is like a genus encompassing what is difficult and otherwise. His saying 'becomes difficult' excludes other than it, so it is not mawat. His saying 'due to lack of water or its overwhelming presence' is an explanation of the cause of difficulty. His saying 'not owned' excludes what is owned, so it is not mawat. His saying 'distant from inhabited area' excludes the near, so it is not mawat. The commentator said: As for the interpretation of mawat land, it is only called mawat if it has this description due to the nullification of benefit from it, by analogy with the dead. The commentator said: This is an apparent interpretation of life. It is said in al-Inaya: Revival legally is that one turns the soil and waters it. If he turns the soil but does not water it, or waters it but does not turn it, it is not revival. In al-Kafi: If he does one of them, it is revival. From Abu Yusuf: Revival is building, planting, turning soil, or watering. From Muhammad: Turning soil is revival. In al-Ghiyathiyya from Muhammad: Turning soil is not revival unless he sows it. From Shams al-A'imma: Revival is making it suitable for cultivation. In al-Khaniyya: If he builds in part of dead land or sows in it, that is revival for that part only, unless what he developed is more than half according to Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said: If the dead land is in the middle of inhabited land, it is revival for all. End quote. Linguistically, revival means causing growth, whether by an act of an agent through purchase or otherwise. It is not said why the author defined mawat and not revival, when it would be appropriate to define both together. We say: He intended to explain the complete description, and he deliberately left the definition of revival. The commentator said: because it is apparent. His saying 'other than owned' means in the abode of Islam because the absolute dead [land] refers to the complete, and its completeness is that it is not owned by anyone because if it is owned by a Muslim or a dhimmi, his ownership remains for lack of what removes it, so it is not mawat. If the owner is known, it is his; if unknown, it is a luqata (lost item) with which the imam deals as he deals with luqata. If an owner appears later, he takes it and holds liable the one who cultivated it if it decreased due to cultivation; otherwise nothing is upon him. The saying of al-Quduri: 'What is ancient' means what has long been in ruin, as if attributed to the people of 'Ad. And the owned in the abode of Islam if no owner is known is considered mawat because its ruling is like mawat since no specific owner is known, though it is not really mawat as we explained. His saying 'distant from inhabited area' is the saying of Abu Yusuf: distant is such that if a person stands at the farthest part of the inhabited area and shouts at the top of his voice, it is not heard; then it is mawat. If it is heard, it is not mawat because the inhabitants of the inhabited area need it for grazing their livestock and throwing their harvests, so their benefit from it is not cut off. According to Muhammad, actual benefit is considered: it is not permissible to revive what the village people benefit from even if distant, and it is permissible to revive what they do not benefit from even if near. Shams al-A'imma relied on Abu Yusuf's saying.

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the chapter on reviving dead lands (Ihya al-Mawat) from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The author first defines al-mawat as land whose cultivation is impossible due to lack of water or its overwhelming presence, which is not owned by anyone, and is distant from inhabited areas. Key Terms
الإحياء (al-iḥyā'): Making land suitable for cultivation by turning the soil, watering, building, or planting, according to various Hanafi authorities.
العامر (al-'āmir): Inhabited land, such as villages or towns, from which the distance of mawat is measured.
الموات (al-mawāt): Land that is difficult to cultivate due to lack of water or its overwhelming presence, not owned by anyone, and distant from inhabited areas.

According to Shams al-A'imma, what is the definition of ihya?
A) Turning soil and sowing seeds.

Defining Dead Land (Mawat) and Its Conditions for Revival
Defining mawat and its revival conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define dead land (mawat) according to the Hanafi school and state the conditions for its revival, including the intra-Hanafi difference on the distance criterion.

Core Idea
Mawat is unowned, distant land; revival with Imam's permission grants ownership.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq defines the key concept of dead land (mawat) in Hanafi fiqh. Understanding its precise conditions is essential for determining ownership rights over uncultivated land. We will parse the legal definition and the criteria set by the Hanafi imams.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two core components of mawat
The land must be (a) not owned by anyone (ghayr mamlūk) in Dār al-Islām, and (b) far from built-up areas (ba‘īdah ‘an al-‘āmir). Land with an unknown owner is treated like mawat for the Imam's disposal.
Land that was owned but later abandoned with unknown owner is not truly mawat but has similar ruling.
2
Understand the criterion for 'far'
Abū Yūsuf defines 'far' as a distance where a shout from the edge of the built-up area is not heard. Muhammad considers actual benefit: if the residents benefit from the land (e.g., for grazing), it is not mawat even if far.
Shams al-A’immah al-Sarakhsī preferred Abū Yūsuf’s view.
3
Note the ruling on revival
Reviving mawat with the Imam’s permission grants ownership. Merely marking (taḥjīr) does not give ownership. Revival means making the land productive (e.g., planting, building, irrigating).
If someone revives part of a plot, only that part is owned (except if the revived part is more than half, per Abū Yūsuf; Muhammad says revival in the center revives all.)
4
Distinguish different categories of abandoned land
Land with no known owner in Dār al-Islām is treated like mawat. However, ruins from the Islamic era with unknown owners cannot be taken (like owned property). Pre-Islamic ruins are like mawat.
This distinction is based on the ruling of Nawādir Hishām and Risāla Abī Yūsuf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب إحياء الموات ومن أحياها بإذن الإمام ملكها وإن حجر لا ولا يجوز إحياء ما قرب من العامر ومن والغراس أو الكرب أو السقي. وعن محمد الكرب الإحياء وفي الغياثية عن محمد: الكرب ليس بإحياء إلا أن يبذرها وعن شمس الأئمة : الأحياء أن يجعلها صالحة للزراعة . وفي الخانية : لو بنى في بعض أرض الموات أو زرع فيها كان ذلك إحياء لذلك البعض دون غيره إلا أن يكون ما عمر أكثر من النصف في قول أبي يوسف. وقال محمد: إذا كان الموات في وسط الأحياء يكون إحياء للكل ا هـ . والإحياء لغة الإنبات سواء كان بفعل فاعل من شراء وغير ذلك، ولا يقال لماذا عرف المؤلف الموات دون الإحياء والمناسب أن يعرفهما معاً لأنا نقول : أراد بيان الأكمل وإنما ترك تعريف الإحياء. قال الشارح: لأنه ظاهر. وقوله «غيره مملوكه» يعني في دار الإسلام لأن الميت الإطلاق ينصرف إلى الكامل وكماله بأن لا يكون مملوكاً لأحد لأنها إذا كانت مملوكة لمسلم أو ذمي كان ملكه باقياً لعدم ما يزيله فلا يكون مواتاً، فإذا عرف المالك فهي له وإن لم يعرف كانت لقطة يتصرف فيها الإمام كما يتصرف في اللقطة، ولو ظهر لها مالك بعد ذلك أخذها وضمن من زرعها إن نقصت بالزراعة وإلا فلا شيء عليه، وقول القدوري فما كان منها عادياً مراده بالعادي ما قدم خرابه كأنه منسوب إلى عاد الخراب عهدهم. وجعل المملوك في دار الإسلام إذا لم يعرف له مالك من الموات لأن حكمه كالموات لأنه لا يعرف له مالك بعينه وليس هو مواتاً حقيقة على ما بينا. وقوله «بعيدة عن العامر» هو قول أبي يوسف والبعيدة أن تكون بحيث لو وقف إنسان في أقصى العامر وصاح بأعلى صوته لم يسمع منه فهو موات، وإن كان يسمع فليس بموات لأنه أهل العامر يحتاجون إليه لرعي مواشيهم وطرح حصائدهم فلم یکن انتفاعهم به منقطعاً. وعند محمد يعتبر حقيقة الانتفاع حتى لا يجوز إحياء ما ينتفع به أهل القرية وإن كان بعيداً، ويجوز إحياء ما لا ينتفعون به وإن كان قريباً، وشمس الأئمة اعتمد قول أبي يوسف وفي التتارخانية : إذا عرف أنها كانت مملوكة في الأول ولم يعرف مالكها الآن قال القاصي أبو علي السغدي عن استاذه الحكم: إنه يجوز للإمام أن يدفعها إلى رجل ويأذن له في الإحياء فتصير لمن أحياها . وفي نوادر هشام : إذا كان بها آثار عمارة من بناء وبئر ولا يعرف مالكها الآن لا يسع لأحد أن يحييها أو يمتلكها أو يأخذ منها تراباً. وفي رسالة أبي يوسف لها رون الرشيد: لمن أحياها وليس للإمام أن يخرجها من يده وعليه فيها الخراج. وروى هشام عن محمد في الكفور الخربة والأماكن الخربة إذا رفع الرجل منها التراب وألقاه في أرضه قال : إذا كان القصور والخراب تعرف أنه من بناء قبل الإسلام فهي بمنزلة الموات لا بأس بذلك، وإن خربت بعد الإسلام وكان لها أرباب لكن لا يعرفون لا يسع لأحد أن يأخذ منها شيئاً لأنها بمنزلة دورهم ا هـ .
Book of Reviving Dead Lands. Whoever revives it with the permission of the Imam owns it, and marking does not [give ownership], and it is not permissible to revive what is close to built-up land... Revival linguistically means causing growth... His statement 'other than his property' means in Dar al-Islam... His statement 'far from built-up land' is the view of Abu Yusuf...
Source pages p. 386

Commentary
This passage defines the legal concept of dead land (mawat) and the conditions for its revival. The author begins by stating the ruling: reviving dead land with the Imam's permission grants ownership, but merely marking it does not. Revival is defined as making the land suitable for cultivation, such as planting, building, or irrigating. The land must be far from built-up areas, with a distance such that a shout from the edge of the built-up area is not heard (according to Abu Yusuf). Land with an unknown owner in Dar al-Islam is treated as dead land in terms of the Imam's disposal, but if ruins date from after Islam and have unknown owners, they cannot be taken. The passage also discusses the difference between land that was originally owned and now has unknown owners, and land that was never owned.

Key Terms
موات (mawāt): Land that is not owned and is far from built-up areas, suitable for revival.
إحياء (iḥyā’): Making dead land suitable for cultivation by planting, building, or irrigating.
بعيدة عن العامر (ba‘īdah ‘an al-‘āmir): Land so far from inhabited areas that a shout from the edge is not heard.
تحجير (taḥjīr): Marking land with stones or signs to claim ownership; not sufficient to own mawat in Hanafi law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as presented in the passage, which of the following is a condition for dead land (mawat) to be revived and owned?
A) The land must be at least one mile from any inhabited area.
B) The land must have no traces of previous construction.
C) The land must be such that a shout from the built-up area is not heard (Abu Yusuf's view).
D) The land must be owned by the state.

Key Takeaway
Mawat is unowned, distant land; revival with Imam's permission grants ownership, but the distance is determined by the auditory test (Abu Yusuf's relied-upon view).

Imam's Permission for Reviving Dead Land: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on Imam's permission for reviving dead land

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether Imam's permission is required for owning revived dead land, explain the proofs of both sides, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Ownership of revived dead land does not require Imam's permission — the relied-upon Hanafi position follows the Sahibayn.

The revival of dead land is an encouraged act in Islam, but a key question arises: does one need the Imam's permission to own the land after revival? This lesson examines the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, on this very issue. You will analyze the proofs from each side and learn which view is adopted for fatwa in the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Start by clearly stating Abu Hanifa's view (permission required) and the Sahibayn's view (permission not required). Recognize that this is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
The issue is about the condition for ownership, not the validity of revival itself.
2
Examine Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa argues that dead lands in Muslim territories are fay' (public treasury) and thus subject to the Imam's discretion, similar to war booty. Therefore, permission is needed for ownership.
The key concept is that the land is considered fay' under Hanafi classification.
3
Examine the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn rely on the hadith 'Whoever revives a land not owned by anyone, he has more right to it' (Bukhari, Muslim). They also analogize to collecting firewood and hunting, which do not require permission.
The hadith is general and unconditional, seemingly supporting their view.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Sahibayn's proof
The commentary points out that the hadith cited for the Imam's position ('A man has only what his Imam is content with') is general but is specified to matters requiring the Imam's discretion, and reviving dead land falls under that due to its status as fay'.
This is a method of takhsis (specification) of a general text.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and the mufta bihi
Under Abu Hanifa, revival without permission does not grant ownership; under the Sahibayn, it does. Later Hanafi authorities, including al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah, prefer the Sahibayn's view as the operative position for fatwa.
The mufta bihi is that no permission is required, making practical ownership easier.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ومن أحياها بإذن الإمام (ملكها وهذا قول الإمام. وقالا : يملك من أحياء ولا يشترط فيه إذن الأمام لقوله لا من أحياء أرضاً ليست لأحد فهو أحق بها» رواه البخاري ومسلم. ولأنه مباح سبقت إليه يده كالاحتطاب والاصطياد. وللإمام قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم ليس للمرء إلا ما طابت به نفس إمامه فإن قلت: اعتبر عموم هذا الحديث يلزم أن لا يملك أحد شيئاً من الأملاك بغير إذن الإمام مع أن الظاهر خلافه كالبيع وغيره. قلت: عمومه غير معتبر بل هو مختص بما يحتاج فيه إلى رأي الإمام وما نحن فيه من قلت: كون ما نحن فيه يحتاج إلى إذن الإمام هو أول المسألة فيلزم المصادرة ولأن هذه الأراضي كانت في أيدي الكفار فصارت في أيدي المسلمين فكانت فيئاً ولا يختص بالفيء بدون إذن الإمام كالغنائم بخلاف المستشهد به فلم يكن فيئاً وإذا أحياها فهي خراجية أو عشرية على ما بينا في السير وبينا الخلاف فيه. قال في الهداية : ملكها خراجية أو فيها العشر لأن ابتداء وظيفة المسلم بالخراج، إلا إذا استقاها بماء أحد له عشرية قال : والو " عن فيها الخراج على اختلاف الماء، ولو تركها بعد الإحياء وزرعها غيره الخراجي لأنه حينئذ سبب قيل الثاني أحق بها لأن الأول ملك استغلالها لها دون رقبتها، والأصح أن الأول أحق بها لأنه ملك رقبتها بالإحياء فلا تخرج عن ملكه بالترك. ولو أحيا أرضاً مواتاً ثم أحاط الإحياء بجوانبها الأربعة أربعة نفذ على التعاقب تعين طريق الأول في الأرض الرابعة في المروي عن محمد لأنه لما أحيا الجوانب الثلاثة تعين الجانب الرابع للاستطراق وفي الظهيرية : فإن جاء أربعة معاً ولم يتقدم أحدهم وأحيا كل واحد منهم جانباً منها وأحاطوا بالأربعة جوانب معاً فله أن يستطرق من أي أرض شاء إذا كانوا أحيوا جوانبها الأربعة معاً؛ هكذا قال والدي ا هـ. ويملك الذمي بالإحياء كالمسلم لأنهما لا يختلفان في الملك . قال تاج الشريعة : فإن قلت : ما رواه عام خص منه الحطب والحشيش وما روياه لم يخص فيكون العمل به أولى قلت : ما ذكر لبيان أنه لا يجوز إلا فتيات على رأي الإمام والحشيش والحطب لا يحتاج فيهما إلى رأي الإمام فلم يتناولهما عموم الحديث فلم يصر مخصوصاً، والأرض مما تحتاج فيها إلى رأي الإمام لأنها صارت من الغنائم بإيجاف الخيل وإرضاع الكلاب كسائر الأموال فكان ما قلنا أولى. وفي الخانية في كتاب الزكاة ذكر الناطفي القاضي في ولايته بمنزلة الإمام في ذلك ا هـ .
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'Whoever revives it with the Imam's permission owns it' – this is the statement of Imam [Abu Hanifa]. And the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] said: He owns it by reviving, and the Imam's permission is not required, because of his statement, peace be upon him: 'Whoever revives a land that is not owned by anyone, he has more right to it' narrated by Bukhari and Muslim. And because it is permissible preceded by his hand like collecting firewood and hunting. And for the Imam is his statement, peace be upon him...
Source pages p. 386

Commentary
This passage presents the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether the Imam's permission is a condition for owning dead land through revival. Abu Hanifa requires permission because the land is ultimately war booty (fay') belonging to the Muslim treasury, and thus the Imam's authorization is needed like in the distribution of spoils. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani argue that the Hadith 'Whoever revives a land that is not owned by anyone, he has more right to it' explicitly grants ownership without permission, and they analogize it to collecting firewood and hunting, which are permissible without state permission. The commentary then addresses objections: the Hadith 'A man has only what his Imam is content with' is limited to matters requiring the Imam's discretion, and dead land revival falls under that due to its status as fay'. The passage also discusses related issues: the land becomes kharaji or ashri depending on water source, and the first reviver retains ownership even if he later abandons it. Dhimmi reviving owns it just like a Muslim, and a governor acts like an Imam in this. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of the Sahibayn, as indicated by the later preference for their view in the commentary.

Key Terms
فيء (fay’): Property taken from non-Muslims without military force, considered public treasury.
الخراجي (al-kharājī): Land subject to kharaj tax.
إحياء الموات (iḥyā' al-mawāt): The act of reviving dead (uncultivated) land to make it productive.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi mufta bihi, which of the following is true regarding reviving dead land?
A) The reviver must obtain the Imam's permission before revival to own the land.
B) The reviver automatically owns the land upon revival without needing permission.
C) Only dhimmis need permission; Muslims do not.
D) The land becomes public property regardless of revival.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that reviving dead land grants ownership without the Imam's permission, based on the hadith and the preference of the later scholars.

The Protected Area (Ḥarīm) of a River: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ḥarīm of rivers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the ḥarīm of a river, identify their proofs, and apply the tarjih to practical cases of river ownership and maintenance.

Core Idea
A river has no ḥarīm by default; need alone does not create a protected area unless supported by text or consensus.

In Hanafi property law, the ḥarīm is a buffer zone around a water source reserved for the owner's use. While wells and springs indisputably have ḥarīm, rivers spark an intra-madhhab debate. This lesson unpacks the positions, proofs, and practical consequences of this disagreement, showing how later authorities settled it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its authors
The matn states 'no ḥarīm for a river' – this is Abu Hanifa's view. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) affirm a ḥarīm on both sides. Note who holds each position.
In Hanafi texts, 'al-Imam' = Abu Hanifa; 'Sahibayn' = Abu Yusuf and Muhammad
2
Analyze the evidence for each view
Abu Hanifa uses istihsan: ḥarīm for wells/springs is text-based (nass) and cannot be extended by qiyas. The Sahibayn argue from need (ḥājah): the river owner requires banks for water flow and mud disposal, just like a well owner.
Abu Hanifa gives the example of a palace in the desert – need alone doesn't grant ḥarīm
3
Extract the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
If a river is dug in dead land, does the owner get a ḥarīm? According to Abu Hanifa, no; according to the Sahibayn, yes. This affects rights to adjacent land for maintenance.
Later texts distinguish between large and small rivers
4
Determine the fatwa position (tarjih)
Al-Kubra states the fatwa is on Abu Yusuf's view (ḥarīm exists). However, for small rivers needing frequent dredging, there is consensus that ḥarīm exists. Also note the measurement dispute: Abu Yusuf says half the river's width on each side; Muhammad says full width.
Tarjih may vary by context – always check the specific case
5
Apply to the scenarios in the text
Work through the examples: disputed dam between river and landowner (al-Jami' al-Saghir), two rivers between villages (al-Fatawa), and planting vs. mud disposal (Abu Ja'far's compromise).
The compromise: planting follows Abu Hanifa, mud disposal follows the Sahibayn

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ولا حريم للنهر) وهذا قول الإمام. وقالا له حريم من الجانبين لأن استحقاق الحريم للحاجة وصاحب النهر يحتاج إليه كصاحب البئر والعين لأنه يحتاج إلى الشيء على حافتي النهر ليجري الماء إذا حبس بشيء وقع فيه إذ لا يمكنه المشي في وسط الماء، وكذا يحتاج إلى موضع يلقي عليه الطين عند الكرب. وفي الكبري : والفتوى على قول أبي يوسف. وهذا إذا حفر النهر في أرض الموات. وفي الكافي ومن كان له نهر في أرض غيره فليس له حريم عند الإمام إلا أن يقيم البينة على ذلك وقالا له مشاة النهر ويمشي عليها ويلقي عليها طينه وفي السراجية قال حسام الدين: والصحيح أنه يستحق الحريم . وفي الفتاوى : نهران بين قريتين وقع الاختلاف في حريمهما فما كان مشغولاً بتراب أحد النهرين فهو في أيدي أهل ذلك النهر والقول في ذلك القدر لهم فلا يصدق الآخرون إلا ببينة، وما كان بين النهرين ولم يكن مشغولاً بتراب أحدهما فهو بين أهل القريتين إلا أن يقيم أحدهما البينة أنه له خاصة قال الشارح: دليل الأمام أن استحقاق الحريم في البئر والعين ثبت نصاً بخلاف القياس فلا يلحق بهما ما ليس في معناهما ألا ترى أن من بنى قصراً في الصحراء لا يستحق حريماً وإن كان يحتاج إليه لإلقاء الكناسة لأنه يمكن الانتفاع بالقصر دون الحريم. وفي الجامع الصغير نهر لرجل إلى جنبه مسناة وأرض لآخر والمسناة في يد فإن لم يكن لأحدهما غرس ولا طين ملقى فادعى صاحب الأرض المسناة وادعاه صاحب النهر فهي لصاحب الأرض عند الإمام. وقالا : هي لصاحب النهر جرى الملقى عليه طينه وغير ذلك فينكشف بهذا اللفظ أن يكون الحريم موازياً للأرض لا موضع الخلاف وهو فصل بينهما وأن لا يكون الحريم مشغولاً بحق أحدهما معيناً معلوماً، وإن كان فيه أشجار ولا يدري من غرسها فهو على الخلاف أيضاً، وكذا قبل إلقاء الطين على الخلاف، والصحيح أنه لصاحب النهر ما لم يفحش . ثم إذا كان الحريم لأحدهما أيهما كان لا يمنع الآخر من الانتفاع على وجه لا يبطل حق مالكه كالمرور فيه وإلقاء الطين ونحو ذلك مما جرت به العادة ولا يغرس فيه إلا المالك لأنه لا يبطل حقه. قال الفقيه أبو جعفر : أخذ بقوله في الغرس وبقولهما في إلقاء الطين. ثم عند أبي يوسف حريمه قدر نصف بطن النهر من كل جانب وهو اختيار الحاوي، وعند محمد مقدار بطن النهر من كل جانب وهو اختيار الكرخي. وذكر في كشف الغوامض أن الخلاف بين أبي حنيفة وصاحبيه في نهر كبير لا يحتاج فيه إلى الكري في كل حين أما الأنهار الصغار يحتاج فيه إلى كربها في كل وقت فلها حريم بالاتفاق اهـ.
He (the author) said: 'And there is no ḥarīm for a river.' This is the statement of Imam (Abu Hanifa). And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It has a ḥarīm on both sides, because entitlement to ḥarīm is due to need, and the owner of the river needs it like the owner of a well and a spring, because he needs a place on both banks of the river to let the water flow if something blocks it, since he cannot walk in the middle of the water, and similarly he needs a place to throw the mud when clearing. And in al-Kubra: The fatwa is on the opinion of Abu Yusuf. This applies if the river is dug in dead land. And in al-Kafi: Whoever has a river in another's land, he has no ḥarīm according to Imam unless he provides evidence; and the two said he has a path for his river and walks on it and throws his mud on it. And in al-Sirajiyya, Husam al-Din said: The correct view is that he is entitled to ḥarīm. And in al-Fatawa: Two rivers between two villages, dispute over their ḥarīm: what is occupied by the soil of one river is in the hands of the people of that river, and the claim over that amount is theirs; the others are not believed without evidence. What is between the two rivers and not occupied by either's soil is between the people of the two villages unless one provides evidence that it is his specifically. The commentator said: The evidence of Imam is that entitlement to ḥarīm for wells and springs is established by text (nass) contrary to analogy, so other things not in their meaning should not be attached to them. Do you not see that one who builds a palace in the desert is not entitled to a ḥarīm even though he needs it for throwing garbage, because he can use the palace without the ḥarīm. And in al-Jami' al-Saghir: A river belonging to a man next to a dam and land belonging to another, and the dam is in hand; if neither has trees or thrown mud, and the landowner claims the dam and the river owner claims it, then it belongs to the landowner according to Imam. And the two said: It belongs to the river owner because he throws mud etc. It becomes clear from this expression that the ḥarīm is parallel to the land, not the place of dispute, and that it is a separator between them, and that the ḥarīm is not occupied by a known right of one specifically. If there are trees and it is not known who planted them, it is also subject to the same dispute. Similarly, before throwing mud, there is dispute. The correct view is that it belongs to the river owner as long as it is not excessive. Then, if the ḥarīm belongs to one of them, whoever it is, he does not prevent the other from using it in a way that does not nullify the owner's right, such as passing through, throwing mud, and similar customary uses. Only the owner may plant there because he does not nullify his right. Al-Faqih Abu Ja'far said: He took his (Imam's) opinion regarding planting and their (the two's) opinion regarding throwing mud. Then according to Abu Yusuf, its ḥarīm is half the width of the river on each side, which is the choice of al-Hawi. According to Muhammad, the width of the river on each side, which is the choice of al-Karkhi. And it is mentioned in Kashf al-Ghawamid that the dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two companions concerns a large river which does not need dredging every time; as for small rivers that need dredging every time, they have a ḥarīm by consensus.
Source pages p. 390

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ḥarīm (protected perimeter) of a river. The author states the base ruling from the matn: there is no ḥarīm for a river according to Abu Hanifa. His two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, disagree, arguing that the river owner needs a ḥarīm on both banks for maintenance and access, similar to a well or spring. The commentator then presents various later sources: al-Kubra gives the fatwa according to Abu Yusuf; al-Kafi distinguishes between rivers dug in dead land (where ḥarīm is denied to the river owner unless he proves a prior right) and other cases. Al-Sirajiyya and al-Fatawa provide further applications, including disputes between two rivers and their owners. The commentator gives Abu Hanifa's evidence: ḥarīm for wells and springs is established by a specific text (nass) and cannot be extended by analogy to rivers, as shown by the example of a palace owner not getting ḥarīm for garbage disposal. Al-Jami' al-Saghir presents a scenario with a river, a dam, and a landowner, showing the disagreement. The passage concludes with the specific measurements of ḥarīm according to Abu Yusuf (half the river's width on each side) and Muhammad (full width), and notes that for small rivers requiring frequent dredging, there is consensus on ḥarīm.

Key Terms
حريم (ḥarīm): The protected perimeter or area around a water source (well, spring, river) that is reserved for the owner's use and maintenance.
نهر (nahr): A river or sizable water channel, distinguished from a well or spring in this context.
الإمام (al-Imām): Abu Hanifa, the eponym of the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in al-Kubra, what is the ruling on the ḥarīm of a large river dug in dead land?
A) No ḥarīm, following Abu Hanifa.
B) Ḥarīm exists of half the river's width on each side, following Abu Yusuf.
C) Ḥarīm exists of the full river's width on each side, following Muhammad.
D) No ḥarīm unless the owner provides explicit evidence.

Key Takeaway
The ḥarīm of a river is a contested right; the fatwa follows Abu Yusuf for large rivers, but small rivers have ḥarīm by consensus.
